# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary of Findings

I've identified **28 key Go source files** implementing the five major ngalert components:

### **Core Components:**

1. **Alert Rule Storage** (`pkg/services/ngalert/store/`)
   - `database.go`: `DBstore` - main persistent storage class
   - `alert_rule.go`: Rule querying methods
   - `instance_database.go`: Alert instance persistence
   - `alertmanager.go`: Alertmanager configuration storage

2. **Scheduler** (`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/`)
   - `schedule.go`: Main `schedule` class implementing `ScheduleService`
   - `alert_rule.go`: Per-rule evaluation goroutine
   - `fetcher.go`: Periodic rule fetching from storage
   - `recording_rule.go`: Recording rule evaluation

3. **State Manager** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/`)
   - `manager.go`: `Manager` class with state cache & transitions
   - `cache.go`: In-memory state caching
   - `state.go`: Individual `State` and `StateTransitions` types
   - `persist.go`: Persistence and `Historian` interface
   - `store_state_reader.go`: Database warm-load on startup

4. **Notifier** (`pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/`)
   - `alertmanager.go`: Per-org alertmanager wrapper
   - `multiorg_alertmanager.go`: `MultiOrgAlertmanager` routing alerts to correct org
   - `receiver_svc.go`: Receiver configuration management
   - `silence_svc.go`: Silence management

5. **History Writer** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/historian/`)
   - `core.go`: Core history recording
   - `annotation.go`: Grafana annotations backend
   - `prometheus.go`: Prometheus remote write backend
   - `loki.go`: Loki backend
   - `multiple.go`: Multi-backend support
   - `backend.go`: Backend abstraction

grafana/grafana comprises five major interacting components:\\n\\n### 1. Alert Rule Storage (pkg/services/ngalert/store/)\\nThe storage layer is implemented by `DBstore` (database.go), a database-backed storage system that persists alert rule definitions and metadata. Key files include:\\n- `database.go`: Main DBstore class implementing AlertingStore and rule persistence\\n- `alert_rule.go`: Methods for querying alert rules via GetAlertRulesForScheduling() and GetAlertRulesKeysForScheduling()\\n- `instance_database.go`: Stores alert instances (individual alert firing states) via SaveAlertInstances() and ListAlertInstances()\\n- `alertmanager.go`: Persists alertmanager configurations\\n\\nThe DBstore is injectable through ProvideDBStore() and serves as the single source of truth for all alert rule definitions across all organizations.\\n\\n### 2. Alert Rule Scheduler (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/)\\nThe scheduler manages the periodic evaluation of alert rules. Key files:\\n- `schedule.go`: Main scheduler implementing ScheduleService interface, created via NewScheduler(). Manages the evaluation loop and rule registry\\n- `alert_rule.go`: Per-rule executor that runs in its own goroutine, fetches evaluation results and sends them to state manager\\n- `fetcher.go`: updateSchedulableAlertRules() fetches rules from DBstore at configured heartbeat intervals\\n- `recording_rule.go`: Handles recording rules (Prometheus-style rules that write metrics)\\n\\nThe scheduler runs as a continuous service (Run() method) that fetches all active rules, detects changes, and spawns/terminates evaluation goroutines. It uses the AlertsSender interface to dispatch firing alerts.\\n\\n### 3. State Manager (pkg/services/ngalert/state/)\\nThe state manager tracks alert states over time and determines state transitions. Core files:\\n- `manager.go`: Manager class managing alert state cache, created via NewManager(). Implements AlertInstanceManager for state queries\\n- `state.go`: State type representing individual alert instance state with fields like Firing, Pending, etc.\\n- `cache.go`: In-memory cache of all current alert states organized by rule and labels\\n- `persist.go`: StatePersister and Historian interfaces for persistence and history recording\\n- `store_state_reader.go`: StoreStateReader reads alert instances from database on startup\\n\\nThe Manager processes evaluation results via ProcessEvalResults(), compares against previous states to determine transitions (e.g., pending\u2192firing), and records state changes. It maintains a cache warm-loaded from the database (Warm() method) and periodically persists state via StatePersister.\\n\\n### 4. Notifier (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/)\\nThe notifier delivers alerts to alertmanager instances and manages silences. Key files:\\n- `alertmanager.go`: Per-organization alertmanager wrapper (alertmanager class, NewAlertmanager()). Wraps prometheus-alertmanager\\n- `multiorg_alertmanager.go`: MultiOrgAlertmanager created via NewMultiOrgAlertmanager(). Manages per-org alertmanagers and routes alerts to correct org\\n- `receiver_svc.go`: ReceiverService manages notification receiver configuration per organization\\n- `silence_svc.go`: SilenceService manages active silences that suppress alerts\\n\\nWhen scheduler dispatches alerts, they flow through MultiOrgAlertmanager which routes them to the correct per-org alertmanager. The alertmanager applies routing rules, silences, and notification policies before sending notifications.\\n\\n### 5. History Writer (pkg/services/ngalert/state/historian/)\\nThe historian records state transitions for audit and querying. Implementation files:\\n- `core.go`: WriteStateTransition() base function for recording state changes with rule metadata\\n- `annotation.go`: AnnotationBackend uses Grafana annotations as backing store\\n- `prometheus.go`: PrometheusWriter writes state history to Prometheus remote write endpoint\\n- `loki.go`: LokiWriter writes state history to Loki\\n- `multiple.go`: MultipleBackend supports multiple simultaneous backends (e.g., primary Loki + secondary Prometheus)\\n- `backend.go`: Backend type abstraction allowing selection between annotation/prometheus/loki\\n\\nThe Historian interface (persist.go) is called by state manager's persistence layer to Record() state transitions. Multiple backends can be active simultaneously, with one designated as primary for reads.\\n\\n### 6. Alert Sender (pkg/services/ngalert/sender/)\\nThe sender routes evaluated alerts to external systems. Key files:\\n- `router.go`: AlertsRouter created via NewAlertsRouter(). Routes alerts to internal MultiOrgAlertmanager and/or external alertmanagers based on admin configuration\\n- `notifier.go`: ExternalAlertmanagerSender sends alerts to external alertmanagers\\n- `sender.go`: Base sender functionality\\n\\nThe router is called by scheduler with alert transitions and determines whether to send to: (1) internal alertmanager, (2) external alertmanager, or (3) both, based on configuration stored in AdminConfigurationStore.\\n\\n### 7. Main Service Orchestration (pkg/services/ngalert/)\\nThe main files that wire everything together:\\n- `ngalert.go`: AlertNG service class providing ProvideService() dependency injection function that instantiates and wires all components\\n- `evaluation_runner.go`: EvaluationRunner manages the lifecycle of the scheduler during instance startup/shutdown\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: ProvideService() creates all components. State manager warm-loads from database via InstanceStore.\\n\\n2. **Rule Evaluation Loop**: EvaluationRunner starts scheduler's Run() method. Scheduler:\\n   - Fetches all active rules via DBstore.GetAlertRulesForScheduling()\\n   - Spawns evaluation goroutine per rule (alert_rule.go)\\n   - At configured intervals, sends evaluation events to each rule's goroutine\\n\\n3. **State Processing**: Each alert_rule goroutine:\\n   - Evaluates the rule (via eval package)\\n   - Sends results to state manager via ProcessEvalResults()\\n   - State manager compares to cached state, determines transitions\\n   - Saves instances to database via InstanceStore.SaveAlertInstances()\\n\\n4. **History Recording**: State manager calls Historian.Record() for all state transitions, which routes to configured backends (annotation/prometheus/loki)\\n\\n5. **Alert Notification**: State manager calls state.Sender (implemented by schedule) which sends firing/resolved alerts to AlertsRouter\\n\\n6. **Alert Routing**: AlertsRouter.Send() determines destination (internal/external/both) and dispatches via:\\n   - Internal: MultiOrgAlertmanager \u2192 per-org alertmanager \u2192 notification receivers\\n   - External: ExternalAlertmanagerSender \u2192 remote alertmanager\\n\\nAll components use consistent models from pkg/services/ngalert/models, maintain prometheus metrics, and support feature toggles via featuremgmt.FeatureToggles.\"\n}\n",

grafana/grafana comprises five major interacting components:\\n\\n### 1. Alert Rule Storage (pkg/services/ngalert/store/)\\nThe storage layer is implemented by `DBstore` (database.go), a database-backed storage system that persists alert rule definitions and metadata. Key files include:\\n- `database.go`: Main DBstore class implementing AlertingStore and rule persistence\\n- `alert_rule.go`: Methods for querying alert rules via GetAlertRulesForScheduling() and GetAlertRulesKeysForScheduling()\\n- `instance_database.go`: Stores alert instances (individual alert firing states) via SaveAlertInstances() and ListAlertInstances()\\n- `alertmanager.go`: Persists alertmanager configurations\\n\\nThe DBstore is injectable through ProvideDBStore() and serves as the single source of truth for all alert rule definitions across all organizations.\\n\\n### 2. Alert Rule Scheduler (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/)\\nThe scheduler manages the periodic evaluation of alert rules. Key files:\\n- `schedule.go`: Main scheduler implementing ScheduleService interface, created via NewScheduler(). Manages the evaluation loop and rule registry\\n- `alert_rule.go`: Per-rule executor that runs in its own goroutine, fetches evaluation results and sends them to state manager\\n- `fetcher.go`: updateSchedulableAlertRules() fetches rules from DBstore at configured heartbeat intervals\\n- `recording_rule.go`: Handles recording rules (Prometheus-style rules that write metrics)\\n\\nThe scheduler runs as a continuous service (Run() method) that fetches all active rules, detects changes, and spawns/terminates evaluation goroutines. It uses the AlertsSender interface to dispatch firing alerts.\\n\\n### 3. State Manager (pkg/services/ngalert/state/)\\nThe state manager tracks alert states over time and determines state transitions. Core files:\\n- `manager.go`: Manager class managing alert state cache, created via NewManager(). Implements AlertInstanceManager for state queries\\n- `state.go`: State type representing individual alert instance state with fields like Firing, Pending, etc.\\n- `cache.go`: In-memory cache of all current alert states organized by rule and labels\\n- `persist.go`: StatePersister and Historian interfaces for persistence and history recording\\n- `store_state_reader.go`: StoreStateReader reads alert instances from database on startup\\n\\nThe Manager processes evaluation results via ProcessEvalResults(), compares against previous states to determine transitions (e.g., pending\u2192firing), and records state changes. It maintains a cache warm-loaded from the database (Warm() method) and periodically persists state via StatePersister.\\n\\n### 4. Notifier (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/)\\nThe notifier delivers alerts to alertmanager instances and manages silences. Key files:\\n- `alertmanager.go`: Per-organization alertmanager wrapper (alertmanager class, NewAlertmanager()). Wraps prometheus-alertmanager\\n- `multiorg_alertmanager.go`: MultiOrgAlertmanager created via NewMultiOrgAlertmanager(). Manages per-org alertmanagers and routes alerts to correct org\\n- `receiver_svc.go`: ReceiverService manages notification receiver configuration per organization\\n- `silence_svc.go`: SilenceService manages active silences that suppress alerts\\n\\nWhen scheduler dispatches alerts, they flow through MultiOrgAlertmanager which routes them to the correct per-org alertmanager. The alertmanager applies routing rules, silences, and notification policies before sending notifications.\\n\\n### 5. History Writer (pkg/services/ngalert/state/historian/)\\nThe historian records state transitions for audit and querying. Implementation files:\\n- `core.go`: WriteStateTransition() base function for recording state changes with rule metadata\\n- `annotation.go`: AnnotationBackend uses Grafana annotations as backing store\\n- `prometheus.go`: PrometheusWriter writes state history to Prometheus remote write endpoint\\n- `loki.go`: LokiWriter writes state history to Loki\\n- `multiple.go`: MultipleBackend supports multiple simultaneous backends (e.g., primary Loki + secondary Prometheus)\\n- `backend.go`: Backend type abstraction allowing selection between annotation/prometheus/loki\\n\\nThe Historian interface (persist.go) is called by state manager's persistence layer to Record() state transitions. Multiple backends can be active simultaneously, with one designated as primary for reads.\\n\\n### 6. Alert Sender (pkg/services/ngalert/sender/)\\nThe sender routes evaluated alerts to external systems. Key files:\\n- `router.go`: AlertsRouter created via NewAlertsRouter(). Routes alerts to internal MultiOrgAlertmanager and/or external alertmanagers based on admin configuration\\n- `notifier.go`: ExternalAlertmanagerSender sends alerts to external alertmanagers\\n- `sender.go`: Base sender functionality\\n\\nThe router is called by scheduler with alert transitions and determines whether to send to: (1) internal alertmanager, (2) external alertmanager, or (3) both, based on configuration stored in AdminConfigurationStore.\\n\\n### 7. Main Service Orchestration (pkg/services/ngalert/)\\nThe main files that wire everything together:\\n- `ngalert.go`: AlertNG service class providing ProvideService() dependency injection function that instantiates and wires all components\\n- `evaluation_runner.go`: EvaluationRunner manages the lifecycle of the scheduler during instance startup/shutdown\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: ProvideService() creates all components. State manager warm-loads from database via InstanceStore.\\n\\n2. **Rule Evaluation Loop**: EvaluationRunner starts scheduler's Run() method. Scheduler:\\n   - Fetches all active rules via DBstore.GetAlertRulesForScheduling()\\n   - Spawns evaluation goroutine per rule (alert_rule.go)\\n   - At configured intervals, sends evaluation events to each rule's goroutine\\n\\n3. **State Processing**: Each alert_rule goroutine:\\n   - Evaluates the rule (via eval package)\\n   - Sends results to state manager via ProcessEvalResults()\\n   - State manager compares to cached state, determines transitions\\n   - Saves instances to database via InstanceStore.SaveAlertInstances()\\n\\n4. **History Recording**: State manager calls Historian.Record() for all state transitions, which routes to configured backends (annotation/prometheus/loki)\\n\\n5. **Alert Notification**: State manager calls state.Sender (implemented by schedule) which sends firing/resolved alerts to AlertsRouter\\n\\n6. **Alert Routing**: AlertsRouter.Send() determines destination (internal/external/both) and dispatches via:\\n   - Internal: MultiOrgAlertmanager \u2192 per-org alertmanager \u2192 notification receivers\\n   - External: ExternalAlertmanagerSender \u2192 remote alertmanager\\n\\nAll components use consistent models from pkg/services/ngalert/models, maintain prometheus metrics, and support feature toggles via featuremgmt.FeatureToggles.\"\n}\n",
